THEMINATION AGREEMENT
The unisereigned hereby acknowledges that a costastual Frolationship
has heretofore existed between him and the Government of the United States
of America (hereinafter referred to as ("the Government").
the Government
has fully and completely satisfied all of its obligations to the undersigned.
The undersigned on behalf of himself, his heirs, executors, administra-
tore and Assigns hereby releases and forever discharges the Government; its
officers, agents and employees from any and all debts, salinas, benefits or
demands arising out of the above mentioned contractual relationship.
The undersigned fully understands and appreliates the fact that the prior
relationship between the parties and all information and knowledge acquired in
the course of said relationship (particularly with reference to persons and
methods employed by the Government) are the proper-t of said Government and
constituta-military secrets affecting its security. The undersigned knowa and
the following: "The Government and the Government under the provisions of
Annex A to the Convention on Rights and Obligations of Foreign Forces in the
Federal Republic of Germany.
The Government is highly appreciative of the excellent services hereto-
fore rendered by the undersigned. However, to preserve the security above
mentioned, it is further understood and agreed that both parties shall here-
after disavow that the relationship ever existed.
The undersigned further agrees he possesses no right, title or interest
in any information or knowledge arising out of said relationship and he fur-
ther solemnly suvears that he will never divulge, publish or reveal by word,
conduct or any other means the fact of said relationship nor any such knowledge
or information arising therefrom except as authorized in writing by the same
official of the Government as that who witnesses this oath.
Frankfortlinman this July of March 196
Georg F. Sandlow
(L.S.)

a

ORNE K. DARONNAT
Case Officer
COMMENTS:
C. O. met Subject in response to a telephone call in
which Subject invited C. O. to lunch to help him celebrate
a new stroke of l'ortune. WIROGUE told C. o. that the
director of the firm in Munich (reported in previous contact
reports) and his European sales representative had met with
Subject and discussed the possibility of his association with
the Munich firm. Subject said the following had been agreed
on:
Subject would receive 1500 DM a month-salary,
free living quarters in Munich, the cost of
maintaining his apartment in Frankfurt, expense
account, and percentage of the profits realized
from any of Subject's inventions patented by the
firm, a work shop in Munich plus absolute personal
freedom of movement regarding working hours, etc.
C. O.
C. 0. told him that the above was very hard to believe,
that he should have this in writing. Subject said that it
was to be drawn-up and sent to him for his signature.
C. 0., of course, expressed his delight with Subject's
perspicacity and perspicuity and 18th but not 100100
gall. C. 0. asked if this would mean he would be moving to
the-Munith-area Subject said that this was doubtful unless
he could find a mechanic in the Munich area who would work
at the same time. The problem was to be done with the
intends to spend most of his time in Munich, however, and
will come to Frankfurt once a month to oversee Nagely's work
on the production models of his projects. Subject intends to
do the research and development work in Munich with Nagely in
Frankfurt making the finished model.

REPORT ON CONTACT WITH AGENT OR DEFECTS
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
DATE:
30 January 1964
TIME:
1000 hours
PLACE:
ANCONGEN
FORME E. DARRONANT. Case Officer
COMMENTS:
C. 0. and Subject met at the American Consulate since
Subject's apartment (DRC's former safe apartment) is being
painted Subject told C.0. he had been staying at the
Balmoral Hotel and would move back into the apartment on
Friday evening, 31 January 1964. C. 0. and Subject went to
the apartment which fs indeed being painted and
reappeared.
C. 0. paid Subject DN 1,000, DN 800 of which is for
subsistence and rent for February and the remaining DM 200
to be applied to the one month's rent in advance required
by the land.
C. 0. told Subject that all copies but one of his original
police reception intervention interview story had been recalled and
the German language version of his Libenslauf was now being
used to provide the basis for a new story. C. 0. told Subject
that as soon as the new story was prepared, copies placed in
the various files and the one remaining copy of the old story
removed from its file, Subject would be, for all practical
purposes.
C. 0. told him that we have decided to help him get a new
start by (1) paying the cost of having his denture; repaired,
(2) by paying DM 200 on the DM 300 one month's rent in advance
Subject must pay, (3) by providing DM 800 per month for
subsistence and housing until he can be legally on his own,
and the other party is not a party. The party is not a
termination and (5) by making him a present of all the household
items now in the apartment including the iron, the vacuum
cleaner, and the radio. Subject's rather perfunctory thank you
was somewhat less than what C. 0. had expected and when C. 0.
expressed surprise at Subject's lack of enthusiasm, Subject
stated that he was most appreciative but was not very demonstrative.
SECE

C: 0. told Subject to obtain receipts for the one month's
retail. The C: 0. and for the February rental payment. He was
also to call C: 0. the check of February 2nd to arrange a
meeting so that C: 0. the pick up the receipts and Subject's
copy of his old political recognition interview story.

140000
27 January 1964
MEMORANDUM FOR: Chief, HARVARD
FROM
: ORME K. DARONNAT
SUBJECT
:
WIROGUE
Don, I suggest that we reduce the quantity of some of
the items listed on the attached and make WIROGUE a present
of the remainder as part of his resettlement.
I have been emphasizing to Subject over the past weeks
that President Johnson's economy drive has affected all
agencies and departments. Subject, therefore, has been
conditioned not to expect money for BKZ or for furniture or
a termination sum. Any or all of these would normally be
provided in a case of this kind.
I feel that if we pay to have his lower denture repaired,
approximate cost DM 400, make Subject a present of the house-
hold items listed, and continue to pay him subsistence for a
month or two after we notify him he is on his own, we will,
I believe, get rid of him as cheaply as possible and without
serious complaints.
Sime

REPORT ON CONTACT WITH ACENT OR DEECTOR
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
DATE:
21 January 1964
TIME:
1200 hours
PLACE:
51 Kuhwaldstr.
ORNE K. DARONNAT Case officer
COMMENTS:
C. 0. met Subject and paid him subsistence for the week
ending 31 January 1964. He was told that we have received
permission to increase his subsistence from DM 600 to DM 800
per month until his final resettlement. The extra DM 200 is
to be applied to his rent: C. 0. said that Subject would bo
paid DM 1000 on 31 January DM 200 to be applied to one
month's rent in advance, and the DM 800 to be rent (DM 200)
and the DM 200 is to be applied to the other.
C. 0. said we were disappointed that he had decided to
stay in his present apartment and take over the DM 300 rent.
We had hoped he would be sensible enough to use this opportunity
to save a little money. Subject's answer was that he feels
that he should be able to afford the rent when he is turned
to the home. The rent was not a result of the rent. The rent
will be dead. Subject said he could not understand why C. 0.
was harping on the subject, that all he was asking for was
one month's advance notice prior to being turned loose on his
time. The rent was willing to drop the matter as long as
Subject did not come from the right to look later about needing
money. Subject said that if things got really bad he would
get a job. C. 0. applauded and offered his congratulations.
but said he assumed this would only be a description of course.
Subject did not like the joke.
WIRGUE proudly announced that he has made intensive
efforts the last few weeks to sell 4 of his inventions. C. 0.,
the right to look at the last would never understand how
such an obviously clever man could, for so many years, refuse
to face up to his responsibilities to himself and society and
live in a dream world of get rich quick schemes. Subject put
on what is now a familiar act in which he acts terribly hurt
because C. 0. (his one true friend) does not have faith in him.
C. 0. told Subject that he is a great actor and added that he
(C. 0.) would think much more highly of him if he would think

REPORT ON CONTECT WITE ASUIT OR DEPECTION
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
DATE:
15 January 1964
TIME:
1115 hours
in
PLACE:
Kuwaldstr.
ORME K. DARONNAT Case Officer
COMMENTS:
c. o. dropped by and informed Subject we will not
be moving him into any more of our housing, that housing
suitable for him is occupied and would not be available
for some time. C: 0. told Subject that he will give him
800 D.B.' month instead of the usual 600. DM. He is to take
the time to be given. He was advised to get economy
housing and try to save the money. He was president's economy
drive was affecting our budget and C. o. to get a new
what kind of help, if any, could be given Subject when he
finally leaves our custody. Many months ago C. o. had
been given a upon his final termination we would see
what help could be in him towards apartment rental, dishes,
furniture, etc. C. o. feel that it would be a good idea.
to tell Subject that he should have a great deal of
help when he leaves us, that he might receive very little,
if any.
C. o. tried to discourage Subject from taking over the
Kuwaldstr apartment, but Subject said he is working on an
invention for the owner of the apartment and would try to
swing some sort of deal. Subject asked if he could expect
to receive some help if he had to pay an ant in advance when
he gets his new quarters. C. o. told him she would pay the
first month's rent in advance but would require the receipt
from Subject.
Subject said he would call C. o. as soon as he has
made arrangements for living quarters for himself.

REPORT ON CONTACT WITH AGENT OR DEFECTOR
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
DATE:
10 January 1964
1130 hours
TIME:
Kuhwaldstr.
PLACE:
CONCENTS:
C. : O. dropped by to see Subject and pay him two weeks
subsistence. Subject asked C. intended to do
regarding housing for him since the sales price is 1.00
apartment would be given up 31 January. C. 0. said he was
aware that the apartment was to be given up and had hoped
to get a month or two extension. C. 0. went on to say that
he felt that it could not be done and that he would talk
to his housing people and would contact Subject early the
following weeks.
C. 0.1, David Subject that his Libenslauf had been completed
and was being translated into German. C. 0. feels that the
final step towards Subject's permanent resettlement can be
taken within the next two months.

140000
7 January 1964
MEMORANDUM FOR THE RECORD
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
1100 hours
On this date Grady Elms, John Spiegler, Don McLaughlin,
Bill Murray and John Wims (Camp King) met to discuss the
WIROGUE case. It was explained to Wims that we have prepared
a Labenslauf for Subject and we are ready to take the next
steps necessary for Subject's resettlement and that we wished
to establish if, as Wims told us some months ago, it would
be possible to prepare a new political recognition interview
story and replace the old copies with the new story. Wims
said it wak would be necessary to recover
odl story, copy, the
Nucernberg copy in the hand of the by, but he
felt that this could be done. It was decided that months ago
when the BND became interested in this case that copies had
probably not been made of the story, only extracts to include
Subject's name, his birth date, probably the names of his
parents and an extract of the reference Subject's activities
with the Georgian Resistance Group. It was decided, therefore,
that this same information should definitely appear in the
new Labenslauf. This was to be taken care of by having
Subject's father's name be Frank Simon Sanders (since Subject's


name is Georg Frank Sanders and on the original story
Subject's father's name is given as Simon Sanders the new
story will indicate. that Subject's father's full name is
Frank Simon Sanders which will explain Subject's middle
name as Frank) in the paragraph referring to Subject's
detection by the: militia so make some reference to Subject's
alleged activities in a resistance group. It is felt that
if Subject's new story ever comes to light in the future,
what was once reported as Subject's activity in a resistance
group will be to have been misread and
alleged activity in a Georgian resistance group. We all
realize that if acopy has been made of the story there is
nothing we can do about it anyway.


REPORT ON CONTACT WITH. AGENT OR DEPECTOR
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
DATE:
13 December 1963
TIME:
1030 hours
PLACE:
Kuhwaidstr.
COMMENTS:
C. 0: dropped in and paid Subject two weeks subsistence
and after a short chat took him to lunch. C. 0.
spent several hours window. shopping and just generally
burning around. Subject's normal was greatly improved as a
result and C. 0. feels the time was well spent.
Subject said that he has been worried; that he knows he
will be turned loose on his own soon and asked C. 0., if
possible, to let him have sufficient notice so he can make
plans. C. 0. told him that he would try to give him at
least one month's notice.

REPORT ON CONTACT WITH AGENT UR DERECTION
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
DATE:
29 November 1963
TDE:
1030 hours
PLACE:
Kuhwaldstr.
Dame K. DARONNAT Case Officer
COMMENTS:
C. o. dropped by, paid Subject two weeks subsistence and
thanked him for his note of sympathy regarding the death of
President Kennedy.
Subject was told that his background story is complete
and that we hoped we would soon be in a position to take positive
steps toward his resettlement. Subject went into a long-
winded explanation of why he thought it was wrong for a man
to pay all his life for a crime when technically he had paid
to the same time. The time of the day, he said, he said, not
Subject's misdeeds have placed certain restrictions on his
activities and nothing could be done to change that. He was
reminded that with a new identity he will be in a position to
establish himself and be a contributing member of society.
Subject's answer-was to the effect that he was not too happy
to be contributing to the time.
C. o. know he would like to be clean as a whistle, be able to
use his true name and go back to France.
C. o. told him that all things considered he could be a
lot worse off and should think about building his future.
Subject then stated that he would repay all the money we
had spent on him C. o. told him that we did not want the
money repayed that he would only foul-up our books. He was
told that the best way for him to repay the debt would be to
work hard and lead a decent life.
C. o. left after promising to have lunch with Subject
soon.

REPORT ON CONTACT WITH AGENT OR DEPECTOR
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
DATE:
15 November 1963
TIME:
1100 hours
PLACES:
Kuhwaldstr
Bents Damst
ORME K. DARONNAT
Case Officer
CONCENTS:
C. 0. dropped in to see Subject, paid him two weeks
subsistence and provided cigarettes and coffee. He was told
that unfortunately we have not finished his legend and it will
be a very good thing. He said he was not very
with the new. Subject said that he hoped that he can get
started soon because he is getting nervous, just hanging around
and not being gainfully employed. He reminded C: 0. that
C. 0. had supposedly promised him DKZ and help on new furniture
and finally moved out on his own. C. 0. reminded him that
C. 0. had not promised him anything at all but had said he,
the C. 0., could find out if any help could be given Subject
in this area.
Subject backed down and then stated that his wish had been
to go to South America and that C. 0. had promised him this
would be arranged. C. 0. told him that our intention had been
noted. He said he was not the same. He said he was
accomplish and the matter would have to be dropped. Subject was
told, as he has been told several times, that if he desires
to go to South America he will have to arrange it on his own
and after he has built up some work experience here in the F.R.

REPORT ON CONTACT WITH AGENT OR DEFECTOR
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
126
DATE:
1 November 1963
TDE:
1100 hours
PLACE:
Kuhwaldstr Apartment
D.
ORME K. DARONNAT Case Officer
COMMENTS:
C. o. dropped in to see Subject, gave him cigarettes and
300 marks subsistence for the next two weeks. He was told
that his legend is just about completed, that it is now being
proof read and that our next step would be to have it accepted
by the German authorities: When this has been accomplished
all obstacles to his final resettlement will have been removed.
Subject said that he had been thinking a great deal lately
about being turned loose on his own in the near future. He
said that he hopes to have his latest invention perfected to
the point where he will be receiving a substantial income at
which he is not a good price. C. o. told him that he
he still is trying every year. He was able to inform going to
work, that he still is placing too much emphasiz on "get rich
quick" schemes. Subject denied that this was the case but

REPORT ON CONTACT WITH AGENT OR DEFECTER
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
DATE:
20 September 1963
TDME:
1130 hours
PLACE:
Kuhwaldstr
Date: 100mm
ORNE K. DARONNAT Case Officer
CONMENTS:
C. 0. met Subject and paid him two weeks subsistence.
Subject was in extremely good spirits and seemed quite pleased
to see C.C. He stated that things are going better and better
for him that the mechaniker with,whom he is working had given
him a new electric razor for having solved a difficult mechanical
problem which had-plagued the shop. for some weeks. Subject
to the problem, he said, "I have been a very good job. He
another device which he had been working on for the mechaniker
had been completed and worked so well it had been sent to a
display in France. Subject said that he is
making more and more concretety among the technical people here
in Frankfurt and the other. He said, "I have been a very good
a good job and won't be able to accept it since he will require
a Lohnsteurkarte and a Versicherungskarte. He then asked C.O.'s
advice as to what could be done regarding this problem. C. o.
sued that he is hoping to have an acceptable Labenslauf completed
in the near future and as soon as that story is substituted for
the old he will have to advise the necessary documents. At that point
he will be free to any thing he wishes as far as work and
housing is concerned.
NOTE: C. o. has the necessary tax and insurance cards in his
possession but will not give them to Subject until his Labenslauf
and legal position in Germany is satisfactory. If C. o. lives
Subject the documents now he would probably go to work and besides
earning money would accept our subsistence without notifying C.O.
the company's business. He is a member of the
complaining, that he was: indeed most grateful for the
he has: received over the past month, but he is just as eager as
we are to be on his own making his way in life. C. o. said he
understood and appreciated this fact and hoped that everything
would be in order within the next couple of months.

3 September 1963
MEMORANDUM FOR: Chief, Stage 1
FROM
Chief, Resettlement Branch
SUBJECT
: LEGEND MATERIAL REQUIRED FOR WIRUGUE'S
RESETTLEMENT
1. Since May 1962 HARVARD has been attempting to
work out a sound resettlement for WIROGUE. Headquarters
had authorized HARVARD to assist Subject in his desire to
immigrate to South America, As the first step in this
program, Subject was interviewed at Camp King and a story
of the 1962 war. The Committee was given a letter to
presented to the German interviewer, Certain details of this
story aroused the interest of the German government and it
was necessary for steps to be taken to kill this unwanted
wants. The Committee was asked to build not in itself have been
too much of a problem, but in the next stage, the President
the procedure to be followed for immigration to South America,
HARVARD learned that applicants are screened very thoroughly,
given aptitude tests, etc. etc. This screening is performed
by the President. The Committee will be given as its mass with
the responsibility for insuring that any immigrant is
thoroughly desirable. It became obvious to HARVARD that
Subject would require a legend sufficient to withstand detailed
interviews and sufficient to qualify hin in some profession
on the basis of his actual ability - - the existing political
recognition story does not provide this.
2. In discussions with Wims and Wagner of the Sixth,
it was decided that a detailed life story should be prepared
by CABEZONE and on the basis of this story a new political

recognition interview should be written which would replace
those copies of the old interview now in the various files.
A Reasonably complete legend previously prepared by Alex
Lembersky is attached and with additional information can
be used almost as is. Since this life story will be notional,
the time to be written up in sufficient detail and
plausible enough to be given to the other person who is
needed for the filling out of various future job applications,
to stand-up under detailed interviews to which he may in the
future be subjected and, if immigration ever takes place, to
be given to the requirements. MARVARD feels that this can only
properly be prepared by the Department of the HARVARD there
fore, requests Chief, Stage I to assign a Stage I. Interrogator
knowledgeable on the Soviet Union to prepare a life story to
include a detailed escape from Georgia to Turkey.
3. We realize that this request could involve considerable
work but due to the peculiar problems inherent in the WIROGUE
case, it is vital that we prepare Subject for a new life as
a completely different person. Only by doing the job properly
now will we be able to place ourselves in a position to
satisfactorily sever subject's dependence upon KUBARK and
reduce to a minimum the need for future contacts.

G. Donald McLaughlin

Case Officer noticed that on the patent application,
Subject was listed as an engineer living at Kuhwaldstr 51.
When Case Officer questioned him regarding the use of this
Kuhwaldstr address Subject said that he felt it was necessary
for the following reasons:
1. While riding with Naegele to the Taunus
one day and passing Camp King, Herr Naegele
had remarked that the Camp was the place where
Americans trained commandos and others for
2. Work of a secret nature:
2. The case officer told Subject may
months ago. The method was led up the
Kuhwaldstr apartment and he Subject wanted to
do everything he could to make. arranged to
establish himself on his own he had decided it
would be best to-use the Kuhwaldstr address
because he would be receiving mail and did not
want to inconvenience Case Officer by having
him be a delivery boy.
3. Subject felt that the use of this address
is not a very satisfactory since he would not use
that address for any special reason, e.g.,
police matters, etc., etc.
Case Officer still reamed Subject out thoroughly and told
him that even though our attempts to maintain maximum security
were probably 50% successful we should at least try. Case
Officer finally realized he was fighting a losing battle
and the other organization, but he would have
more difficulties for the child Subject they might as
well drop the subject. Subject kept the right that he would
do nothing to jeopardize what Case Officer's organization was
trying to do for him and assured Case Officer he thinks out
very carefully what the results of any particular case of
action.
Case Officer told Subject that he is trying to make
his legend and once everything is in order with the Complete
government Subject would be in a position to establish himself.
Case Officer told him that it is obvious his hopes for
immigration to South America should be she/led for a good long
time, that it would appear obvious Subject should establish
himself here in Germany building up a work background and then
if he so desired, immigrate. This would be without our help.

CO. dropped in to see Subject and found him in an
exceptionally good mood.
He remarked that he was beginning to feel like a charity
case and asked how long he would be on our hands. CO
told him that there were three possibilities:
1. Subject could stay right here in Germany, find
himself a job and CO would find out what help
Headquarters would provide in the way of help toward
an apartment and furniture.
2. Subject would have to study Russian for six months,
since it is impossible for anyone to have been
raised and worked in the Soviet Union without knowing
some Russian. At the end of that time he would try
to make a new way. (Subject was not told this but
it is obvious that if he had been able to get out
once he gets to S.A., the first Russian he comes in
contact with will realize he is not a bona fide
refugee which would lead to trouble for Subject.)
3. There is a possibility he could be gotten to Chile.
(John Wills has suggested that through his contacts
he might be able to get Subject to Chile, since the
Chilean Ambassador owes him a favor.)
CO told Subject to think about the three possibilities
and make and give CO his thoughts on the problem the next
time they meet.

gone before the Government changed it's attitude toward refugees.

Columbian Government would probably check with the Soviet Gov't to

his being put in prison for entering the country under false pretenees,

the Sovs. Subject would arrive a bone fido immigrant fully checked

Case Officer worked with Subject discussing the vital
statistics which would have to acquired for and memorized by
Subject in order to supply the refugee organization with
certain factual information necessary for his position with
This information would also be vital if in casual conversation
Subject was to keep from drawing suspicion to himself when

Subject would need. Subject asked if with his name could it

Baltic countries. C/O promised to find out and inform him at
their next meeting.
28 February
1100
C/O dropped in to see Subject and informed him that he
would very likely be processed for South America through a
refugee organization. This would mean with a refugee organ-
ization behind him and USEP support he would not be subjected
to the investigation, interviews, etc he would normally undergo
if he went directly to ICEN.
C/O told Subject that arrangements would be made for him
to start studying Spanish as soon as practical.
Subject was told that his name was a common one throughout
the Baltic region and therefore, he would be able to discuss
that part of his legend with confidence.

for the refugee to appear at I CEM in Bad Codesburg until the final
actees of the processing.

Concerning Georg SANDERS, gmbxx6xix born 25 July 1919
in
Tifils/USSR. Present residence in Oberursel/Ts,
Hobenzirstr. 145.
Cross reference, none,
As of the 14th July 1962 SANDERS is in the custody
of an U.S. organization in Oberursel. It was alleged
that he had arrived on the same date as a tourist from
East- to West Berlin and deflected there.
On the 28th of August 1962 he filed application for
recognition as a foreign refugee.
On 29 August 62 he was interviewed; in the presence
of a member of a U.S. organization, by the criminal
investigation. During the interview SANDERS made
untrained for the 1962, he was asked to accept the
Among other SANDERS said that he had been leading
member of a resistance group in the Soviet Union. More-
over he claimed that he evaded arrests by joining a
Soviet tourist group with the assistance of friends.
The tourist group went on a guided tour of the
Soviet occupied East zone of Germany. The group left
Tifils on the 10th of July 1962 arriving in East Berlin
on the 14th of July 1962. Subject claimed that upon
arrival to East Berlin he escaped immediately. However,
the U.S. refused to make more detailed statements about
his escrow to West Berlin. Allegedly it was unknown to
him how his friends had managed to place him into the
tourist group.
We would be grateful if any communications or
information concerning SANDERS inclusive a possible
interview report would be forwarded to us.

S E C R E T
MEMORANDUM FOR THE RECORD
29 January 1963
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
On this date George List and the undersigned discussed
CO's plans and thinking regarding WIROGUE's immigration to
South America. Case Officer explained that since Subject is
an exceptional case and not a bona fide refugee, we will not
be able to take advantage of the normal immigration channels
without taking the chance of being involved in fraud. Case
Officer further explained that since WIROGUE's contact with
the Consulate of his choice will not in any way be controlled
by us, this immigration attempt will be a one shot operation
and if it fails, we will not have a second chance because if
he is turned down for immigration, any subsequent attempts he
makes to immigrate will bring to light the fact that he had
previously applied for immigration to another country. It is
essential therefore that we plan for every contingency. Case
Officer feels, based on HARVARD's experience, that when WIROGUE
applies for immigration he will be required to give
(1) the name and address of his present employer and
probably the name of his supervisor and telephone number.
(2) what type of work he has been doing;
(3) proof that he will be able to support himself for
a minimum of two years at the rate of $125 a month.
(4) proof of his professional qualifications.
(5) birth certificate.
(6) detailed information regarding his employment and
residence addresses in the Georgian SSR
(7) details of the war-time military service.


S E C R E T
-2-
Case Officer said that early next week he will meet with
Wagner and Wills of the 513th and explain the above. If it
is possible he will get them to agree to provide the details
of (1) above in the event the Consulate should call as part
of the routine immigration processing. (2) above will be taken
care of in the same manner. Regarding (3), Headquarters has
given us authority to expend up to $3,000 and Case Officer will
513th of this. They will be asked to provide a letter
if required, stating that Subject has been associated with
them (whatever cover organization they wish to use) since his
defection in July 62 and has roughly $3,000 in salary and bonuses
being held for him. Regarding (4) whether or not is is adviseable
to provide Subject with proof of his professional qualifications
will be discussed with the 513th. (5) above, a birth certificate
will probably not be necessary since so many defectors do not
have these documents with them. Information on employment and
residences will be worked up by the Case Officer from past.
defector's BARs and with material available to SR 6. (6) above -
this information may also be acquired through facilities of SR 6.
After discussions with the 513th, Case Officer will tell
WIROGUE that we have been informed by Headquarters that if
Subject still desires to immigrate to South America and is
successful in immigrating, we have authority to provide financial
assistance during the transition period up to $125 a month.
Since Case Officer knows WIROGUE, the next question will be,
How long will I receive this $125 a month? Case Officer will
reply, Until you become satisfactorily established or we have


reason to believe that you are not sincerely trying to establish
yourself. Case Officer will tell him,
it were necessary.

9 January 1963
MEMORANDUM FOR THE RECORER
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
Case Officer received a letter from Chuck Pettit, addressed
to WIROGUE (George Sanders), Hohmarkstr. 45. See Officer
opened the letter and found it to be from a Lt. Zircle of the
Transportation Corps. The Lt. mentioned that he was offered
to the Chief of the conversation with Subject at the Bahnson
short-time ago and had found him very interesting. The Lt.
said he received a letter on the cell of plesasure from meeting people
such as Subject with such interesting backgrounds.
He suggested that he and Subject meet for dinner in the
near future.
Case Officer took th letter to Bob Bullock, told him a
little bit. The Subject's past and suggested that something
be done to provide a letter from continuing his friendship with
Subject, since Case Officer took that WIROGUE would probably
use the Lt. for whatever he could be. He said. Bullock
said he would have CID contact the Lt. and tell him a lay off
for his own good. Bullock promised to find out if the
had given Subject his address and to advise him that if he
is left run into Subject, he should not mention having written
a letter.
Rame
ORNE K. DARONNAT

REPORT ON CONTACT WITH AGENT: OF EFFECTR
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
DATE:
3 January 1963
TDC:
1515
PLACE:
Kuhwaldstr. 55
CONCEMS:
Case Officer dropped by to see Subject and pay him
subsistence to 19 January. Subject is in good spirits
and does not seem as restless. He usually is. He
confided to. Case Officer that be hoping he won't have
to do any running around regarding immigration as
long as the weather stays as bad as it. He seems to
be reasonably-satisfied with his lot in life and only
asked that the Case Officer drop by a little more often
if possible because he gets lonely.
S-E-C-R-E-T
S-E-C-R-E-T
ORNE K. DARONNAT Case Offider


#2 the Strasse
Frankfurt a. Main
3 January 1963
Mr. Georg Sonders
157 Pocrmark Str
Oberursel
Parrkfurt a. Main
Dear Mr. Sanders:
Just wanted to drop ou this line to tell you again how much I
enfoved our conversation the other evening at the Bahnhof. My greatest
experiences in Germany are the different people I meet, and it is always
very pleasant to talk with someone such as yourself who has such an
interesting background.
My friend felt rather silly at his attempted joke. The next time
he either will have less to drink or will think more before alowning!
It would be a pleasure to see you arain durin- my tour of duty
in Prankfurt. Maybe if you have a free hour or so in the future you
would want to have another supper in the Bahnhof!
MEMO ROUTING SLIP
VPER USE FOR APPROVALS
Sincerely,

S-E-C-R-S-T
REPORT ON CONTACT WITH ACENT OR DETECTOR
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
DATE: 19 December 1962
TDE: 1030
PLACE: 51 Kuhwaldstr.
Dank Pome
ORNE K. DARONNAT Case Officer
CONENTS:
Case Officer dropped in to deliver some Christmas cheer
to Subject and gave him his Reiseauscis and Anmeldebestatigung.
His HARVARD Identity document was picked up:
Subject told Case Officer he had the feeling that Head-
quarters would advise us to turn him loose without any additional
information us and he was worrying because it would be difficult
for him to get the message. The case officer was not
officer told him that we are aware of this and that if it is
recommended that he be resettled on the economy we are not in
the habit of throwing people out in the street and that we would
do. everything we could to help him become integrated.
Subject was paid subsistence for two weeks. Case Officer
promised to try to drop by the end of next week.
From time to time Subject tries to find out if Case Officer
knows the details concerning Subject's past work for us and the
reasons for our insistence that he was blown in the Congo. (A
fact which he does not believe and therefore feels that the
relationship was discontinued for other reasons.) Case Officer
had to be able to be did not know and did not wish to know the
details since the tobacco paper now could what is necessary
for us to resettle the people for how we are responsible.
S E C R E T


REPORT OR CONTACT WITH AGENT OR DEFECTOR
SUBJECT: WIROGUE
DATE:
1000
TIME:
51 Kuhwaldstr.
PLACE:
COMPENTS:
Case Officer dropped by to see Subject, who seems to be
in good spirits and busy making preparations to make appli/
cation for a patent on one of his brain-storms.
Subject was told that the details of his case had been
submitted to Headquarters, that we were now prepared to move
based on Headquarter's advise. Subject was told that we can
only wait for the answer from Headquarters.
Subject has requested a German typewriter which will be
delivered to him some time this week.
S E C R E T
28 November 1962
5
ORME K. DARONNAT, Case Officer

for the case factories specializing in small electrical devices. The mans
name is Will be not a patent address is Frankfurt/Main, an Tiergarten 52,

Parkstr. 13, telephone 559165.
Subject told Case Officer that if he is lucky and his invention is
successful prior to any definite arrangements we make for his immigration
to South America, he will leave our custody and probably stay right here
in:Frankfurt. He said that he is aware he has committed himself to go to
South America and will do so but all that he wishes to do if immediate
situation of his motion is not forthcoming, is to get a patent on his
question so he cannot be given to the patent. He said.
Case Officer feels that this is about the best we can expect from
Subject. Case Officer has discussed this situation regarding the patent
with John Morrison of the legal staff, who says that he will at least try
to find out if this patent attorney is qualified and successful.
NOTE: Case Officer has learned that the patent laws in Germany are somewhat
peculiar in that a patent attorney is a technical qualified man who can
be used to make the patent. He said he has specialized and for which he
has received: a specialized education of the patent attorney in the case
that he can deal with any legal questions which arise in the patent
patent procedures or litigation in patent matters. Normally, an individual
who intends to get a patent will hire an attorney who will contact a patent
attorney. Between the two of them they can handle all problems and procedures
involving a patent. This also can be worked in reverse.

BIOGRAPHY OF GEORG FRANK SANDERS
1. IDENTITY:
A. FULL NAME: Georg Frank SANDERS
B. NAME AT BIRTH: Georg SANDERS: as featured in my birth
certificate and all other Soviet documents. However,
upon arrival in the West, I added to my first name the
name of my father, Frank. While in the USSR when the
French Civic was required; I was referred to as Georg
Frankovich SANDERS.
C. OTHER NAMES USED: I never used any other names but I
was called by my mother by a Georgian, diminutive "Zhor1",
and by my Russian friends Zhora or Zhorzh".
2. BIRTH:
A. DATE OF BIRTH: 25 July 1919
B. PLACE OF BIRTH: Tiflis, Georgia, USSR. Tiflis is the
old Russian name. The Georgian as well as the present
official name is Tbilisi.
C. NATIONAL ORIGIN: Georgian
3. CITIZENSHIP:
A. AT BIRTH: Soviet. From 1917 (October Revolution in
Russia) until 1921, Georgia was governed, from the
downfall of Czarist regime, by Menshevists and partially
occupied by Turk, German and British troops. Only in
1921 did the Soviet government in Georgia officially
trem to power. However, all persons born during this
transition period were classified later as Soviet citizens.
B. PRESENT CITIZENSHIP: Stateless
4. RELIGION: Orthodox (pravoslavnyy). Being raised in a godless
society, I practiced my religion to a very limited extent in
my youth, and, due to existing conditions in USSR stopped
going to the Church in my adult life.
5. SOCIAL ORIGIN: Intelligentia (sluzhashichy); my father was
an engineer, and my mother - a white collar worker.


-2-
6. PROFESSION: Electro-technician, an equivalent of German
'Ingeneur without diploma' (no college graduate)
A. LAST.OCCUPATION: Chief electrician (starshiy elekto-
tekhnik) with MIKHA-TSKHAKAYA RTS.
7. LAST RESIDENCE: Shota Rustaveli Street (ultisa), #25
(private home of my common-law wife, Nina GANDELI) in
MIKHA-TSKHAKAYA; Kutaisi Oblast, Georgian SSR.
8. MARITAL STATUS: Single. From 1946 to the time of my escape
with the same a compon-law marriage with Nina GANDELI, see
TAKTASHYIN: The 2020, When I first got to know her, she
was married to a post-ago employee but her marriage was
an unhappy one. Her husband was a friend and the marriage
had been arranged by her parents, old fashion and
a distant village who were happy to marry their daughter off
the day. She was a friend and well-to-do man. By the time I
was drafted into the service of the 11 were lovers. When
I returned from the war, I moved in with the husband
had been killed in action during World War II and she
was a daughter born during this time, in a small home
inherited friend. She was a friend Her parents were dead, and she
worked as a mail carrier for her husband. He was a friend
During the later years of our life together, I like education.
That Nina was having affairs with other men. This caused
that she was a friend at home, and made my life unbearable.
Finally, the woman became pregnant, and since I was positive
that it was not my child. I decided to end our relationship
This was one of the reasons for my defection. I have no
children of my own.
9. PARENTS:
A. FATHER: Frank SANDERS, born circa 1885 in the Baltic
area, came to Russia proper circa 1910 and worked a
civil engineer in the Baku, Batumi, and Thilisi area.
In 1918, he married my mother in Thilisi. He died in
1924 of an accident at his place of work. I do not
reamber my father at all, but knew from my mother that
he was a very good and kind man, and was well liked.
B. MOTHER: Maria SANDERS, nee KANTCHELI, born circa 1885 in
the
1911 village. near the Azerbaijania border in Thilisi
Oblast. She was an only child, and when her parents died
of old age, within a few years of each other, she moved to
Tbilisi worked as a clerk in various private enter-
prises until she married my father. After her husband


-3-
died, she went back to work. She changed her place of
employment several times and the only job I can remember
was her. last employment as a cashier with the shoe-
repair shop (artel) on-Sovetskaya. Ultisa in Tbilisi.
She-died in 1934 of a heart attack.
10. BROTHERS AND SISTERS: None at present. I had a brother Leon
born 1923 who died some six months after his birth.
11. OTHER RELATIVES: I knew that my father had relatives in the
Baltic area but our family had no contact with them and I
did not know any of them. I had no close maternal relatives,
and the distant relatives in my mother's home village had no
certain many family disapproving my mother's marriage to
a 'foreigner of another faith. I 'never visited the home
village of my mother.
12. CLOSE FRIENDS AND ASSOCIATES: I never had any real close
friends, but I was somewhat closer to the following persons
in town:
(1) Director of RTS, who was transfered in 1959 to Rustavi,
Georgian SSR.
(2) Rayon veterinarian who had his office in the rayon
veterinary clinic and travelled extensively in the rayon
area visiting collective farms.
(3) Club librarian (a girl friend)
13. SPECIAL SKILLS: I like to invent gadgets and built up a
relatively good home work shop
14. LANGUAGES: Georgian - native
Russian - from school and contacts with
population in Russian speaking
area and in the service.
German - from school and residence in Germany
English - from Technicum, home study and
association with Americans in
Germany.
15. FINANCIAL STATUS: None

and MARDZHAKISHVILISIA Streets; respectively.) 1927,

The most of the students were: Georgia, Russian
language in the 1930s, was given two hours a week. Reagan,
one hour a week, until 1930. I completed seven and foreign
this school and then studied to the death of my mother; at
a technical where I would have given board and quarters
1934-1938 - Tbilisky Elektroy, which, in which the
Ultsa in Tbilisi, in a two-story building with a yard where
1934, hops and the students' hostel building with a yard where
1934, was given an application to this school. In summer
with the seven-year-old certificate and a photo completed
or August I passed the electronic examinations consisting of
Mathematics, Physics, written exam preparation and Russian
research. They name posted on the school bulletin board
I knew I had been accepted, I paid no tuition for seven
a small stipend just through for a bare living. The house given
accommodations where I had been completed with three other students
near the one. On the first floor of a technical building,
where the school office, was located a three separate
quality cereals could be bought cheaply. The needs was of poor
annex on the female students of the school lived in a small
technicum. The same street, two or three blocks were the
For four years I studied physics, mathematics, history, and
and literature. Georgian language and literature, Russian language
Soviet Union, and from 1936 or 1937 - Constitution of the
level. Specialized subparallel subjects were on a high school
technology of metals, theories given at the technicum were
generalis, electrical machines, electronics, strength of
geometries and why), electrical measuring instruments, electrical
The students were also given military and physical training.
Classes ran from September to July of each year, summer
recesses I spent usually in near-by kolkhozes in Kroup
organized by the technician to help out farmers with their
crops,
Examinations were held twice a year, prior to New Year and at

the end of second semester, and were graded by the following
system:

The first three were passing grades.
In the spring of 1938, I took the final examinations, oral
and written, and was issued a diploma. It was a one-page
certificate and indicated that I had attended the technicum
for 4 years. It listed the grades I had received on the
various subjects and showed that I was graduated as an
excellent.
All graduates were assigned to various places of employment
where they had to stay not less than two years. This is a
form of repayment for the money which the government spent
on their education. I was sent to the MIKHA-TSKHAKAYA M.T.S.
which in 1958 was converted into an H.T.S.
17. EMPLOYMENT HISTORY:
1938 - 1941 and 1946 - until defection - - Mikna-Tskhakaya
M.T.S., (Machine-Tractor Station), later converted into R.T.S.
(Repair Technical Station) - Machino-Traktornaya and Remontno-
Tekhinicheskaya Stantsiya, respectively. Mikna-Tskhakaya,
referred to by the population simply as Tskhakaya, was the
first-order of Tskhakayskiy Rayon being renamed so after the
famous College of the United States. The students held name
of the town was Akhal-Senaki and Akhal-Senakskiy and
respectively). M. Tskhakaya was one of the organizers of the
Georgian Communist Party. The town has now about 10,000
years. The school located on the RR line Samtredia-Sukhumi
(the main connection with the 1938-1940) and was
junction to Poti, the Black Sea resort. The town is located
between two large-trIBUTaries of the Rion River: Tsvii and
Terakhi Rivers. On the latter, located a few kilometers
from Mikha Tskhukaya; is situated a small hydro-power station
where I was a part-time employee upon my return from World
War If.


-6-
At the M.T.S. (which was in 1958 converted into R.T.S.
after the machines and equipment were distributed to
the local grain and grape producing collective farms
with the sole responsibility of the food these machines
left with R.T.S.) I soon became the following:
In the large-scale electrical parts for those agricultural and
bridge or electro-mechanics responsible for the maintenance
of the electrical parts for those agricultural and
other machines. My starting salary was 400 or 500 rubles,
but it was missing rapidly and when I was drafted into
the aray, my salary was almost doubled by that time.
For personal reasons I returned to this town after my
discharge from the service, and obtained my old job.
I
described people as electro-technician with the above
described people as electro-which supplied power for the town
and the rest of the rayon. The biggest single-end this second
job since there was a lack of qualifying. It after
the end of the war. I worked in the second shift in the
first year from 1947 until 1953 (when the position was
filled by a youth of 100% of Kutaisi technicum) earning
700 rubles in addition- to my salary with the R.T.S.
Prior to my escape, my income was about 120 new rubles
before deductions. I also had some additional week-end
income from repairing electric household appliances,
radios, etc., for the local citizens. The old currency
was converted 10 to 1 in 1961.

my qualifications as a car driver (I learned how to
operate an automobile while working on electric detail
on car repair at my M.T.S.). I can not recall the unit
number where I went through the basic training. At that
time the bar were full of troops, basically infantry
and artillery units which rotated quite frequently.
E. SPECIALIZED COURSES: One month's driver's training as
mentioned above:
F. RESERVE STATUS:
Summer 1939
Rejected from the active duty for
medical reasons and given reserve
status.
Fall 1946
Discharged from the army and after
submitting my travel and discharge
papers to my Rayvoyen and the needed
a new military booklet which contained
an' indication of my reserve status. I
was never recalled for military train-
ing or duty of any kind after my final
discharge from the service.
G. CHRONOLOGY OF MILITARY SERVICE:
In a group of other enlisted men, I was sent by train to
the 2nd battery of the 253rd separate anti-aircraft
delivery division (OZAD-ogne-zashchintny artilleryiski
division) and using officer of the battery was Lt. VAKS,
Commander of the vzvesting Administration platoon)
of the division was Lt. ENDELADZE. Department of
commander for political affairs was Capt. CHOKHA and
the 2nd battery was Senior Lt. SAMARIN. Major Vlado
(Vladimir) GUROSE and the commanding officer of OZAD
and in February 1943 he was also working at the
of the PVO (protivo-vozduchnaya oborona or anti-aircraft
defense) in the town of Michurinsk. The headquarters of
the 2nd炮, located in Michurinsk, while the battery
itself was started near the station TARASOVO near the
settlement of Konsden, which was a risk of risk and 6 km.
from the six marshalling yards located at Kochetovka
station. A higher HQ was in Tambov and was at first
commanded by Col. CHERNYAVSKIY and later by Col. TSVETKOV,
a demoted General.
When I first arrived in Michurinsk, I was assigned as a
truck driver with the division's supply platoon (khoz-vzvod


-8-
or khozyavystvenny yzvod) commanded My Junior Lt. MAKAROV,
but later I made the acquaintance of the above mentioned
ENDELADZE, a countrym, and through a matter's intervention
was assigned as a personal driver to division commander
GURGENIDZE, also a Georgian, who was promoted to Lt.
Col. and who kept me with him until I was discharged from
the services.
H. PROMOTIONS AND DENDOTIONS: After six months in the service,
I was promoted to: :freytor (corporal), and at the end
of my first year to Junior Sergeant. In 1944, I was made
a sergeant.
I: DECORATIONS: None
J. DATE OF DISCHARGES: I was discharged from active military
duty at the end of September 1946. I received my travel
orders and per diem funds at my unit. I have suriinsk and
turned them in at my rayvoyenkomat. In 1955, I was given
another medical check-up by orders of the voyage at and
discharged from the reserve for medical reasons (same as
before) and issued a so called belly biel (white ticket
or permanent deferment from service).
19. RASIDENCES FROM DIRTU:
1919 - 1926
Several addresses in Tbilisi
1926 - 1934
Tbilisi, Kirochnaya Ulitsa #25, an
apartment in a two-story house; formerly
a private house, later taken over by
the State ZHAKT (housing organization)
enterprise. After my mother's death,
I entered the local electro-technicum
and moved to the students' dormitories.
1934 - 1938
Tbilisi, Ulitsa Sovetskaya, # not recalled,
student hostel of Tbilisi Electro-Technicum.
1938 - 1941
Mikha Tskhakaya, Ulitsa Tsulukidze, #14.
Here I rented a room in a private one-
story house of a retired RR switchan,
Ilya LONDONZÉ, who had to rent a
work with the boarders to
supplement his pension. Ilya's wife, Keto
(Catherine), for an additional charge
took care of my laundry and cooked for me.
The couple had no children of their own
and treated me as their own son.


-9-
1941 - 1946
Army Service
1946 - 1962
Mikha Tskhakaya, Ulitsa Shota Rustaveli,
(until defection)
#25, the private home of my common-lap
wife, Nina GANDELI. I was in love with
her and had an affair with her before
I went to war. During the war, I found
that the most husband was killed in
action and decided to live to Tskhakaya
to be near her: I moved in with
and continued to live with her without
registering our marriage at the local
regional registrar office for marriage;
deaths, the family and though I insisted
on legalizing our union. Nina was always
opposed, being unhappy 13 first
marriage, and wanted to feel free to end
the relationship at any time.
For the last several years Nina, as I
found out, was meeting other men during
the last year, I had been. A rift between
us developed and grew up. I had with
the passing of time. Being deprived of
Nina's intimacy, I reacted by dating other
girls. We were on the verge of separation
and the same time. I had been. I tried
desperately to resolve our problem. Since,
when I still was very close to Nina,
made anti-regime remarks on several
years. I had even planned a joint escape
from the USSR.
In the same time, I was have
her too much in order not to push her into
possibly reporting me to the militia.
However, for some reason Nina did not
be able to have the right completely,
and one day announced that the expect-
ing a child and wanted to legalize our
marriage. Since, I did not consider
myself the father of the child and
fearing black-mail by Nina, I decided to
speed up my defection which I was planning
anyway.
20. TRAVEL:
None except as described previously.


-10-
21. HISTORY OF ARRESTS:
In June 1962, I was approached by the rayon militia at my
place of work and was taken to the militia offices where
I was accused of being a long standing member of a
Georgian resistance group and of making anti-government
of the military forces. He was a senior president of the
occasions and was therefore guilty of the latter charge; I
noticed that the militia did not have sufficient information
on this subject and I denied all accusations. I could not
be aware of the problem of the report. After prolonged
interrogation, during which he was asked to be asked on
my biography, parents, army service, contacts, etc., I was
released with the warning that I was not to leave the
area for the time being and that I would be contacted in the
near future by the militia. Except for this case, I was
never arrested or detained by militia or security organs.
22. MEMBERSHIP IN POLITICAL PARTIES OR ORGANIZATIONS:
I never belonged to the Communist Party. I was urged to
join the Komsomol in 1937 while at the Tbilisi Elektro-
Technicum, and was sponsored there by two of my class-mates,
each of whom had more than two years of Komsomol standing.
I have been the most important role in the military forces
(cell) and at a general meeting of the cell members my
application was discussed and I told my life story and answered
questions put to me by the members. After I was accepted,
I would be asked to help card in about two months from the
city rayon committee of the military forces. I would be
I had to attend meetings and pay very small dues. I never
held any official position with the Komsomol organization.
When I left Tbilisi, I had to deregister from the Tbilisi
Eck, I would be asked to help the military forces organization at my
new place of residence in Mikha Tskhakaya. I would be
to by the local population simply as 'Tskhakaya'). The same
procedure had to be repeated upon my departure to and
discharge from the army (deregistration from the old
organization and registration at the new place). Upon my
time, I am for the army to Tskhakaya, I never registered with
the organization.
When I started to work in Tskhakaya, I was automatically
enrolled in the prof-soyuz (trade unions) where I was a
passive member paying my dues (something like 1% of my salary)
to the trade union organizer of MTS (prof-org) and attending
the obligatory meetings from time to time. I never took
any advantage of trade union members privileges such as the
cut-rate accommodations in rest homes (putevka v dom otdykha).


-11-
23. CONNECTIONS WITH ANY INTELLIGENCE SERVICES:
I never had any contacts with intelligence services. I was
never approached to serve in any capacity for Soviet security
organs.
24. DEECTION AND-ESCAPE:
A. MOTIVATION:
In spite of being born and raised in a Communist country,
the U.S. government, "began to understand that real freedom
did not exist for the individual. It also clear to
me that personal advancement did not depend on the
integrity but on the degree of one's political activity.
I analyzed the Communist lies seeing reality: so different
from the official propaganda. During and after the war,
the U.S. government has been countries and was able
to benefit from the particles of the U.S. government
life there from the even sometimes very carefully worded
reports of those people. After I purchased a good radio
station, I had 56, I started to listen intensively to
foreign broadcasts, and I had a positive activated the
idea of eventual escape from the USSR where the
relatives, no family, no possibilities for advancement
and sent life. My anti-government sentiments which
developed the U.S. government for stronger and stronger,
and it became more and more diffuser to me to hold
myself back and not to express them upon which I did
anyway on several occasions. My involvement with the
militia and the unfavorable developments if my personal
life accelerated my plans for defection.
B. TECHNIQUES OF ESCAPE:
On 25 June 1962, three days after my experience with the
militia, I left my residence at 0700 as I normally would
to go to work. I walked out of town toward Santredia.
And my regular clothing, had 80 rubles and a small
hand, and a little bit of time. I had a train being afraid
of militia surveillance. After I walked at the three kilo-
meters on the highway, I got a ride on a truck from the
near-by collective farm which was headed in the same
direction. I got off the truck downtown in Santredia and
paid the driver one ruble, then walked toward the railroad
station. Here I purchased the ticket for Batumi and
background the train at 1150 arriving in Batumi at 1415. I


found a safe place and slept until dark. I started off
on foot from Batuni and following the sea shore until I
reached the old shooting range about 1/2 or 2 km to
the south. Here I entered the water about 2200 hours;
after destroying my passport (the rest of the patents,
the first at home) and burying my clothing and bags.
knew from the first and second, map. at home that I had to
swim some 18 km, to Turkish and the 18 km. swam all night
and was not sure if I had reached Turkish and the 18 km.
being exhausted, I came ashore at about 0300 or 0400 hours.
The 18 km is stepped out was on the gradient of a
steep slope. There was a lot the silhouette of a hut and
went in. There was an old, most electric motor in
the hut. From the Russian description of the 18 km
underbrush that I was still in Russia. I hid in the
underbrush and spent the rest of the night and
the following day the head was hit was getting dark, I
climbed the slope to observe the 18 km. I walked for a
while hearing voices in Russian coming from the
1 continued back object on the sea which resembled a submarine.
2300 hours I entered the shore and around 2200 or
off shore and then parallel to and started to swim 3 km
range of a search light which swept the 18 km. I came into the
hand, and I had surface the search light swept over me
but nothing happened. I knew I had not been discovered.
I continued to swim until I had already exhausted, and
several hours before dawn went ashore along the a cave
remained there being rocks in the sea near the shore.
up the slope where I saw a wind, The next morning I climbed
grave. I went in and observed the structure resembling a
trapped wing. I saw a large village which I later formed
was Kemal-ning. I thought at first that a minaret was
an observation tower. I was presumed that this was the
village of Sarpi, still on Soya, I had to tell I was very
thirsty and climbed down the hill to a near-by- and to
the 18 km. I met an 11 or 12 year old boy whom I
addressed in Russe. I had to be boy drew away from me. Being
still not sure as to where the wind is the stream
for a while to hide my footprints. The wind is the
underbrush until it grew dark. I came out and went around
the 18 km. The opposite end. There I entered the town
and knocked on the door of a house situated on a hillside.
I called out in this main. Even though I heard voices and
footsteps in the fashion, I opened the door. I climbed
on the roof of a sort of study in the courtyard and spent
the night there. Early next morning I was awakened by
-12-


-13-
noises in the courtyard. I saw several women and two
men. I approached them and tried to make time under-
stand by sign language that I had come from Russia.
I said some persons carrying sticks and axes came
into the course of the machine. I said I had a great I came
from-Russia and wanted to remain in Turkey. The most
took me to the military authorities in Kemal-Pasha,
When I dived into the sea in Batumi, I was wearing swimming
trunks, a belt and a pair of fins. There was a clasp
knife in my belt, a sack needle for stinging myself in
case of a cramp, my money in a nylon bag, three bars of
chocolate, a compass and two Phenamin tablets to increase
the amount of separate nylon bag. Except for the
occasional search light in the sea, which I avoided by
diving, I did not encounter any other obstacles on my way.
I did not inform anybody about my escape plans and did not
receive any help from anybody.
From Kemal-Pasha where I was given some clothing, I was
taken by car to Erzerum and from there by train to
Istanbul refugee center. I was there about a week and
was taken to Germany with the assistance of US authorities
on Friday 6 July 1962.
25 DOCUMENTS:
A. PASSPORT:
I received my first three-year passport at #17 militia
(passport desk) office of Molotovsky rayon of Tbilisi,
where I resided at that time. The passport was a single
sheet of paper with my photo and biographic data on it.
In 1939 I exchanged it for a new five-year passport at
#17 militia, I had been the same in the same form of
a regular booklet form and along with my photo and bio
data, had a stamp of propiska (registration with militia)
which stated the date of my arrival in this town and my
residence address. When I was drafted to the army, I
were a very good candidate for the first year. I had
rayovgenkomat, and picked it up upon discharge from the
service. At that time I received a new five-year passport
from the same militia office with the propiska showing
my new address. In 1951, I exchanged my passport for the
new one which was valid for 10 years and which was
exchanged for another 10-year passport in 1961.


-14-
B. MILITARY BOOKLET (Toymeny Bilet)
See paragraph 18.5 in the army. I had a service booklet
(Sluzhebnaya. knizika) which if turned in. to my rayon
toyenkoma tupon return from the army
C
LABOR/POOKLET (Drudovay Kitzaki)
I never possessed one since it was issued by one employer
and turned in to the new employer. when an individual
changed employment I never changed jobs

Doral
Case Officer and
introduced as Mr. Joseph LORTON, went to
see Subject with the express purpose of discussing the various possibilities
that might be available to document Subject-as legally as possible.
Subject told CO that he had made contact in Department under the name of
de. Panashbet. with a firm that was interest in the United States. The
him that since he did not have a patent this would pose a problem and offered
him 5,000 DM for his idea. Subject told them he would give it to them outright
for $10,000. Although they did not refuse his request, they told him they
would think it over and discuss it with the boss and would have to make a
patent search which would take up to a weeks. Subject told them to go ahead
to the committee. The committee was given these were ways of proving
that the idea was his and he could offer it to other firms. Subject will
now wait to be contacted by this firm.
Case Officer told Subject that we had not heard anything from Headquarters
regarding his re-employment by us. He asked if there was some way of finding
out approximately how long it would take. CO told his this was very difficult,
but we would see if we could make an educated guess.
Subject asked for a key to the mailbox since he will be receiving mail
from his friends in Dortmund and possibly from the firm which he has contacted.
then began discussing documentation with Subject along the following
lines:
The type of documentation he would receive if any would depend upon the
final decision from Headquarters as yet not received. We solicited suggestions
from Subject as to solutions to the documentation problem. Apparently his
immediate desire is to receive back his Australian pass, finish his business
in Europe and return to the Congo to clean up matters there.

Sonner 1934 suchte ich um Aufnahme in dieser Schule an
und überreichte das Schulzeugnis der sieben absolvierten
Jahre und ein Photo. Im Juli oder August bestand ich die
Aufnahmeprüfung über Mathematik, Phrsik und schriftliche
und mutdliche Prüfungen in georgischer und russischer Spra-
che. Als mein Name auf der Aushergetaiel der Schule auf-
schien wusste ich, dass ich besanden hatte, Ich müsste
kein Schulgeld bezahlen und bekam ein Stipendium welches
gerade üles lebensnotwierige deckte. Der Aufenthalt im
Schulheim, wo ich ein Zimmer mit drei anderen Studenten
teilte,war frei. Im ersten Stock des Technikums, in der
Nähe des Schuburos, war ein Speisesaal wo man billig es-
sen könnte. Das Essen war schlecht. Die weiblichen Studen-
ten lebten in etrem Nebengebüpde in derselben Strasse, zwei
oder drei Häuserblocke vom Technikum.
Vier Jahre studierte ich Physik, Mathematik, Geschichte,
Englisch, georgische Sprache und Literatur; von 1936 oder
1937 an die Verfassung der Sowjet Union. Die Gegenstände
wurden auf dem Stand einer"Höheren Schule" gelehrt. Dann
gab es noch die folgenden spezialen Unterrichtsgegenstän-
de: Technologie der Metalle, Theorie der Mechanik, Material-
stärke, Elektn-Maschinen,elektrische Arbeitsverfahren,
Elekto-Geräte, eléktrische Messinstrumente, Zeichnen. Die
Studenten-vurden auch militärisch ausgebildet und körper-
lich ertichtigtt. Der Unterricht dauerte von September bis
Juli. Die Sommerferien verbrachte ich gewöhnlich auf einem
Kolchos mit einer Gruppe,die vom Technikum organisiert wor-
den war, um den Bauern mit der Ernte zu helfen.
Die Prüfungen fanden zwei mal im Jahre statt, vor dem Jahres-
ende und am Ende eines zweiten Semesters. Noten wurden nach
dem folgenden System gegeben:


-7-
5 - Otilitschno. (sehr gut)
4 - Choroscho. (gut)
3 - Posredstwemo (gentigend)
2 - Plocho. (schledt)
1 - Otschen plocho (senn schieds)
Die ersten drei Noten waren notwendig um versetzt zu werden.
Im Frühling 1938 hatte ich Abschlussprüfungen, mindlich und
schriftlich und ich bekam ein Diplom ausgehändigt. Das Zeug-
nis war.eine Seite lang und brachte zum Ausdruck, dass ich
das Technikrum 4 Jahre lang besucht hatte. Es enthleit die No-
ten für alle Gegenstinde und zeigte, dass ich als electro-
mechanic ausgebildet worden war.
Allen Prüflingen wurden verschiedene Arbeitsplätze zugewiesen
an denen sie mindestens zwei Jahre zu verbleiben hatten. Das
ist eine Art von Rückzahlung des Geldes, das die Regierung für
die Ausbildung ausgegeben hatte. Ich wurde MICHA-ZCHAKAJA
M.T.S. zugewiesen; der Name wurde 1958 in R.T.S. abgewandelt.
17. BERUPLICHER WERDEGANG:
1938-1941 und 1946-bis zur Flucht MICHA ZCHAKAJA M.T.S.
(Maschinen-Traktoren-Station), später abgewandelt in R.T.S.
(Reparatur-Technische-Station) ( ( Matchino-Traktornaja und bzw.
Remontno- Technitscheskaja Stanzija ). MICHA-ZCHAKAJA wurde von
der Bevölkerung einfach Zchakaja genannt und war Rayon-Zentrum
des Zchakajskii Rayon, so genannt nach dem berühmten georgischen
Revolutionär MICHA ZCHAKAJA (( der alte Name der Stadt war
ACHAL -SENAKI bezw. ACHAL - SENAKSKII Rayon ). M. Zchakaja war
einer der Organisatoren der georgischen komrunistischen Partei,


-8 -
Die Stadt hat gegenkritig ungefähr 10,000 Einwohrer und be-
findet sich an der Eisenbahnstrecke Samtredia-Suchum1 ( die
Hauptstrecke zwischen Tbilisi und Koskau mit Abweigungen nach
Poti, dem Badoort am Schwarzen Meer. Die Stadt liegt zwischen
zwei Zufüssen des Rion Plusses: Tisii und Terachi. Am Letzteren
liegt ein paar Kilometer von M. ZOKAKAJA entfernt ein kleines
Elektrizitätswerk wo ich nach meiner Rückkehr aus dem II. Welt-
Krieg zeitweilig arbeitete. Bei W.T.S. ( welche 1958 in R.T.S.
umbenannt wurde nachdem die Einrichtungen und Maschinen den
lokalen Getreide-und Trauben- erzeugenden Kolchesen zugeleilt
worden waren und als einzige Verantwortung die Reparatur die-
ser Maschinen mit R.T.S. verbliet). Tich wurde bald Vorarbeitet
einer Gruppe von Elektro-Mechanikern, die für die Pflege und
die Reparaturen der elektrischen Teile von landwirtschaftlichen
und anderen Maschinen verantwortlich waren. Kein Anfangsgehalt
war 400 oder 500 Rubel, sberge stieg schnell und als ich in die
Armee einberufen wurde war mein Gehalt schon fast doppelt so
hoch.
Aus persönlichen Gründen kehrte ich in diese Stadt zurück, nach+
dem ich aus dem Kilitärdienst entlassen worden war und ich er-
hielt meine alte Stellung wieder. Ich bekam dazu noch eine
Stelle als Elektro-Techniker mit dem vorher erwähnten Elektri-
zitätswerk, welches Elektrizität für die Stadt und dem thirigen
Rayon erzeugte. Ich erhielt diese Stelle zugewiesen, da nach
den Krieg ein Mangel an qualifizierten Arbeitskräften bestand.
Ich arbeitete in der zweiten Schicht im Elektrizitätswerk von
1947-1953 ( dann wurde die Stelle von einem jungen Absolventen
des Kutaisi Techrikums gefüllt). Ich verdiente dort 700 Rubel
neben meinem Grundgehalt bei R.T.S. Vor meiner Flucht war mein
Einkommen ungefähr 120 neue Rubel Brutto. Ich hate zusätzliches
Einkommen von Wochenend-irbeiten für die Reparatur von Haushalt
gegenständen,Radios usw. durch Einwohrer der Stadt. Das Geld war
1961 10 zu 1 abgewertet waden.

MILITARISCHER WERDEGANG
A.
REGISTRIERUNG FUR MILITARDIENST: Im Sommer 1939
wurde ich von meinem rayor-wojenkomat ( Rekrutierungs-
stelle) benachrichtigt, dass ich mich an einem bestimm-
ten Tag dort einzufinden habe ; von dort ging es mit
einer Gruppe anderer. zukünftiger Rekruten zu der rayon
polyclinic für die medizinische Untersuchung. Ich habe
den linken Daumen und Zeitgefinger bis zum ersten Glied
durch einen Arbeitsunfall verloren und als dies dem Re-
krutierungsstelle mitgeteilt wurde, wurde ich fur den
aktiven Dienst als ungeeignet erklärt und der Besser
zugewiesen. Zu demalen Zeitpunkt wurde mein pripienoje
widetelstwo ( Registrierungs-Dokument ) für ein Sold-
buch ausgetauscht.
B. ENZIEHUNGSTAG: Ungeführ am 26 August 1941 wurde
ich aufgefordert mich am 27. August beim raywojenkomat
zu melden. Ich tat das und wurde aufgefordert mich zum
Dienst am folgenden Tag zu melden. Mit einer Gruppe von
ungefähr 80 bis 100 Rekruten meines Rayons fuhren mir mit
dem Zug von Thilisi nach Baku, wo die Gruppe in der so-
genannten Saljanskije Kaaparmi ( S. Kaserne ) untergebracht
vurde, die sich am Stadtrand von Baku, auf der Strasse
nach Saljani und zur iranischen Grenze, befand.
C. militärische EINHEIT und ENKENNUNGSNUMMER: Ich diente
bei der Luftabwehr Artillerie. Eine Erkennungsnummer hat
es bei der sowjetischen Armee nicht gegeben.
D. GRUNDAUBILDUNG: Meine erste militärische Ausbildung
erhielt ich in der Saljani Kaserne in Baku und sie dauerte
zwei Monate. Einen Monat reguläre Grundausbildung und im
zweiten Monat verbesserte ich meine Qualifikation als
Autofahrer ( Ich hätte gelehnt wie man einen Wagen fährt
während ich in der M.T.S. die elektrischen Reparaturen

nicht mehr in der ich meine Grundausbildung erhieht. Zu
diesem Zeitpunkt waren die Kassernen überfüllt, meistens
Solänen der Infantrie und Artillerie die iriner wieder
abgelöst wurden.

wuchsen als die Zeit verging. Nachdem das
Verhältnis mit Nina sehr fühl geworden war,
fing ich an mich mit anderen Prauen zu tref-
fen. Wir waren oft daran uns endgültig zu
trennen, aber wir fanden immer wieder zu-
sammen. Ich versuchte verzweifelt unser
Problem zu lösen,denn ich hatte zu einem
Zeitpunkt als wir uns noch sehr nahe waren
Bemerkungen gegen die Regierung gemacht und
ich plante sogar eine gemeinsame Flucht aus
den USSR. Ich wollte sie nicht zuehr ver-
tirgern um sie nicht womöglich dazu zu brin-

nicht gänzlich mit mir brechen und eines


- 14 -

michte. Da ich mich aber nicht als der Vater

Plucht, die ich ohnehin schon geplant hatte, zu
beschleunigen.
20.
REISEN:
Keine anderen als schon erwähnt.
21.
VERHAFTUNGEN:
Im Juni 1962 kam diehilitia zu mir und bracht mich von meinen
Arbeitsplatz zu ihrer Dienststelle wo ich beschuldigt wurde
ein langjähriges Mitglied einer georgischen Widerstandsgruppe
zu sein und regierungsfeindliche Ausserungen gemacht zu haben.
Obwohl ich solche Bemerkungen bei verschiedenen Gelegenheiten
gemacht hatte und deshalb schuldig im Sinne des letzteren Teils
der Anschuldigung war, konnte-ich fühlen, dass die Militia nicht
gentigend Informationen besass und ich verneinteähle Anschuldi-
gungen. Ich konnte mir nicht denken wer dahinter steckte. Nach
langen Verhören, bei denen ich über alle Einzelheiten meines
Lebens, Eltern, Militärdienst, Kontakte, u.s.w. befragt wurde,
wurde ich mit einer Warning entlassen das Gebiet nicht zu
verlassen und es wurde mir gesagt ich würde wieder von der
Militia hören. Kit dieser einigen Ausnahme bin ich nie ver-
haftet oder verhört worden, weder bei der Militia oder anderen
Sicherheitsbehörden.
22.
MITGIEDSCHAFT IN POLTISCHEN PARTEIEN ODER ORGANISATIONEN:
Ich gehörte niemals der kommunistischen Partei an. Mir wurde
nahe gelegt 1937 Konsomol beizutreten während ich am Tbilisi


-15-
Elektro-Technikum war. Dabei wurde von zwei Klassenkameraden
die Bürgschaft übernommen, jeder von den beider war schon
mehr als zwei Jahre Mitglied. Ich reichte mein Gesuch bei
der lokalen Komsomol jatschelka (Zelle) ein und bei einer
Zusammenkunft der Zellenmitglieder wurde mein Aufnahmege-
such besprochen, ich erzahlte meine Lebengeschichte und
beantwortete Pragen. Nachdem ich aufgenommen worden war
erhielt ich meine Mitgliedskarte in ungefähr zwei Monaten
vom Stadt-Rayon-Komittee des Thilisi Komsomol; darauf hin
besuchte ich Versammlungen und zahlte kleine Beitrag. Ich
hatte niemals eine offizielle Position bei Komomol. Als ich
Thilisi verliess musste ich mich von der Tbilisi Organisation
streichen lassen und mich am neuen Wohnort Micha Zehikaja
( bei der Bevölkerung gewhnlich nur "Zchakaja" genannt),
neu eintragen lassen. Dasselbe geschah als ich in die Armee
eintrat ( Austreichen aus der ülten Organisation und Ein-
schreiben am neuen Wohnort). Als ich nach der Entlassung von
der Armee wieder nach Zhakaja zurückkehrte liess ich mich
nicht wieder in die lokale Organisation eintragen.
Als ich in Zhakaja zu arbeiten begann wurde ich automatisch
in die (prof.-org) Gewerkschaft eingeschrieben, in der ich
ein passives Mitglied war, das seine Beiträge ( etwas wie
1% neines Gehaltes ) an den Organisator der Gewerkschaft
von MTS bezahlte und von Zeit zu Zeit einer Pflichtversamm-
lung beiwohnte. Ich machte nie Gebrauch von den Vorteilen
der Mitgliedschaft wie ermässigte Preise in Erholungsstütten
( putewka v dom otdicha ).
23.
VERBINDUNGEN MIT EINEM SICHERHEITSDIENST:
Ich hatte nie einen Kontakt mit einer Sicherheitsbehörde.
Ich wurde auch nie aufgefordert in irgendeiner Art für den
sowjetischen Sicherheitsdienst zu arbeiten.
